<div class=ttime>
<div class='restrict' id='restrict0' onclick='restrict(0)'>PrEP<br><!-- PrEPP --><span style="color:#00b200;nobackground-color:#fff"><span class=posp>100%</span></span><!-- e --></div>
<div class='restrict' id='restrict1' onclick='restrict(1)'>PEP<br><!-- PEPP --><span style="color:#00b200;nobackground-color:#fff"><span class=posp>100%</span></span><!-- e --></div>
<div class='restrict' id='restrict2' onclick='restrict(2)'>Early<br><!-- EarlyP --><span style="color:#00b200;nobackground-color:#fff"><span class=posp>100%</span></span><!-- e --></div>
<div class='restrict' id='restrict3' onclick='restrict(3)'>Late<br><!-- LateP --><span style="color:#006c00;nobackground-color:#fff"><span class=posp>61%</span></span><!-- e --></div>
<div class='restrict restrictsel' id='restrict4' onclick='restrict(4)'>All<br><!-- AllP --><span style="color:#008500;nobackground-color:#fff"><span class=posp>75%</span></span><!-- e --></div>
<div class='restrict headp'>&nbsp;&nbsp;<!-- studies --><span class=studies>65</span> studies<span class=desktop>&nbsp;(<span class=studies>39</span> peer reviewed)</span><!-- studies -->
<span class=headd><br>&nbsp;&nbsp;COVID deaths: <span id=p100 class='save2 odometer'></span></span></div>
</div>

<div class=sumdiv>
<div class='ssummary hidden' id='sum0'>Pre-Exposure Prophylaxis (PrEP) studies are very positive. <span class=ssumb>Positive/negative effects vary in nature, degree, and certainty, please read the papers or descriptions thereof for more details.</span></div>
<div class='ssummary hidden' id='sum1'>Post Exposure Prophylaxis (PEP) studies are positive. One study reports a lack of significance, but analysis shows significance, <a href='boulware.html'>see detailed explanation.</a> <span class=ssumb>Positive/negative effects vary in nature, degree, and certainty, please read the papers or descriptions thereof for more details.</span></div>
<div class='ssummary hidden' id='sum2'>Early treatment studies are very positive. <span class=ssumb>Positive/negative effects vary in nature, degree, and certainty, please read the papers or descriptions thereof for more details.</span></div>
<div class='ssummary hidden' id='sum3'>Late treatment studies are mixed, with effectiveness from slightly negative to very positive. Generally no significant harm except with higher than typical dosages. <span class=ssumb>Positive/negative effects vary in nature, degree, and certainty, please read the papers or descriptions thereof for more details.</span></div>
<div class='ssummary' id='sum4'>Global HC<span class=hs> </span>Q studies. PrEP, PEP, and early treatment studies show high effectiveness, while late treatment shows mixed results.</div>
</div>

<td class="ratd stage">PEP</td>
<td class="ratd ref"><span class=author>Mitjà</span> et al., medRxiv, doi:10.1101/2020.07.20.20157651 (Preprint)</td>
<td class="ratd title">A Cluster-Randomized Trial of Hydroxych<span class=hs> </span>loroquine as Prevention of Covid-19 Transmission and Disease</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x1 class="xatr xpep  hidden">
<td rowspan=5 class="xatd date"><div class=rotate><div class=rotate2><b>7/26</b></div></div></td>
<td rowspan=5 class="xatd xresult resultinc"><div class=desktop>Inconc.
</div><div id=rm1 class="mobile resultmob"><div class=resultmob2>INCONC.</div></div></td>

<td colspan=3 class="xatd xstage"><div class=desktop>Post Exposure Prophylaxis study
<span class=ul>&nbsp; <a target=_blank href='https://www.medrxiv.org/content/10.1101/2020.07.20.20157651v1'>Source</a>
 &nbsp; <a href='mitjapep.html'>Study Page</a></span>
</div><div class=mobile>Post Exposure Prophylaxis study</div></td>
</tr>

<tr id=x1b class="xctr xpep  hidden">
<td class="xctd xref" colspan=3><span class=author>Mitjà</span> et al., medRxiv, doi:10.1101/2020.07.20.20157651 (Preprint)</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x1c class="xctr xpep  hidden">
<td class="xctd xtitle" colspan=3>A Cluster-Randomized Trial of Hydroxych<span class=hs> </span>loroquine as Prevention of Covid-19 Transmission and Disease</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x1d class="xctr xpep  hidden">
<td class="xctd xsummary" colspan=3>Death rate reduced from 0.6% to 0.4%, RR 0.71, not statistically significant due to low incidence (8 control cases, 5 treatment cases).<div class=sspace></div>For positive symptomatic cases, a greater effect is seen for nursing home residents, RR=0.49, vs. overall 0.89, possibly because the exposure events are identified faster in this context, versus home exposure where testing of the source may be more delayed.<div class=sspace></div>Enrollment was up to 7 days after exposure, median 4 days. Treatment delay is unclear. The exposure event timing is not detailed. It appears to be based on the date of a positive test for a contact, which is likely to be much later than the actual exposure time. 13.1% were already positive at baseline, which is consistent with the actual exposure time being significantly earlier. PCR testing has a very high false-negative rate in early stages (e.g., 100% on day 1, 67% on day 4, and 20% on day 8 [1]), hence it is likely that a much higher percentage were infected at an unknown time before enrollment. Medication administration is not detailed. Sensitivity and specificity of the tests is not provided.<div class=sspace></div>Given the delay identifying index cases, PCR test delay, and PCR false negative rate at early stages, the treatment delay in general was very long and could be over 2 weeks.<div class=sspace></div>The RR for non-PCR positive at baseline is 0.74. Including the PCR-positive at baseline patients reduced this to 0.89. This is also consistent with earlier treatment being more effective.<div class=sspace></div>The paper does not mention zinc. Zinc deficiency in Spain has been reported at 83% [2], this may significantly reduce effectiveness. HC<span class=hs> </span>Q is a zinc ionophore which increases cellular uptake, facilitating significant intracellular concentrations of zinc, and zinc is known to inhibit SARS-CoV RNA-dependent RNA polymerase activity, and is widely thought to be important for effectiveness with SARS-CoV-2 [3].<div class=sspace></div>This study focuses on the existence of symptoms or PCR-positive results, however severity of symptoms is more important. Research has shown HC<span class=hs> </span>Q concentrations can be much higher in the lung compared to plasma [4], which may help minimize the occurrence of severe cases and death.<div class=sspace></div>There is a treatment-delay response relationship consistent with an effective treatment, however the authors only provide 3 ranges and do not break down the earliest treatment delay times.<div class=sspace></div>The definition of COVID-19 symptoms is very broad - just existence of a headache alone or muscle pain alone was considered COVID-19. There was an overall very low incidence of confirmed COVID-19 (138 cases across both arms). There were no serious adverse events that were adjudicated as being treatment related. Authors exclude those with symptoms in the previous two weeks, however, those with symptoms up to several months before may still test PCR-positive even though there may be no viable virus.<div class=sspace></div>There appears to be incorrect data. Table 2, secondary outcomes, control, hospital/vital records shows that 8 of 1042 is 9.7% (we get 0.8%).<div class=sspace></div>In summary, this study appears positive in the context of very delayed treatment and very small sample sizes, however we have classified it as inconclusive for now pending further analysis and feedback. Preliminary analysis. Supplementary Appendix is not currently available. Please submit any corrections or comments.
<div class=footnotes><div class=footnote><a target="_blank" href="https://www.acpjournals.org/doi/10.7326/M20-1495">[1] acpjournals.org/doi/10.7326/M20-1495</a></div>
<div class=footnote><a target="_blank" href="https://www.mdpi.com/2072-6643/9/7/697">[2] mdpi.com/2072-6643/9/7/697</a></div>
<div class=footnote><a target="_blank" href="https://www.infezmed.it/index.php/article?Anno=2020&numero=2&ArticoloDaVisualizzare=Vol_28_2_2020_192">[3] infezmed.it/index.php/article?Anno=2020&numero=2&ArticoloDaVisualizzare=Vol_28_2_2020_192</a></div>
<div class=footnote><a target="_blank" href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC7122276/">[4] ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC7122276/</a></div></div>
</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x2c class="xctr xprep  hidden">
<td class="xctd xtitle" colspan=3>Prevalence and clinical correlates of COVID-19 outbreak among healthcare workers in a tertiary level hospital</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x2d class="xctr xprep  hidden">
<td class="xctd xsummary" colspan=3>Study of hospital health care workers showing HC<span class=hs> </span>Q prophylaxis reduces COVID-19 significantly, OR 0.30, p=0.02. 94 positive health care workers with a matched sample of 87 testing negative. Full course prophylaxis was important in this study which used a low dose of 400mg/week HC<span class=hs> </span>Q (800mg for week 1), so it may take longer to reach therapeutic levels. Actual benefit of HC<span class=hs> </span>Q may be larger because severity of symptoms are not considered here but HC<span class=hs> </span>Q may also reduce severity.
</td>
</tr>

<td colspan=3 class="xatd xstage"><div class=desktop>Late treatment study
<span class=ul>&nbsp; <a target=_blank href='https://www.nejm.org/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMoa2019014'>Source</a>
 &nbsp; <a href='cavalcanti.html'>Study Page</a></span>
</div><div class=mobile>Late treatment study</div></td>
</tr>

<tr id=x3b class="xctr xlate  hidden">
<td class="xctd xref" colspan=3><span class=author>Cavalcanti</span> et al., NEJM, July 23, 2020, doi:10.1056/NEJMoa201901 (Peer Reviewed)</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x3c class="xctr xlate  hidden">
<td class="xctd xtitle" colspan=3>Hydroxych<span class=hs> </span>loroquine with or without Azithromycin in Mild-to-Moderate Covid-19</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x3d class="xctr xlate  hidden">
<td class="xctd xsummary" colspan=3>Late stage RCT of 667 hospitalized patients with up to 14 days of symptoms at enrollment and receiving up to 4 liters per minute supplemental oxygen, not finding a significant effect after 15 days.<div class=sspace></div>Authors note: &quot;the trial cannot definitively rule out either a substantial benefit of the trial drugs or a substantial harm&quot;, sample sizes are too small.<div class=sspace></div>The paper uses the terms mild and moderate, however all patients had serious enough disease to be hospitalized, and 14% were actually randomized in the ICU.<div class=sspace></div>The trial had significant protocol deviations and unusually low medication adherence. Randomization resulted in 64.3% male patients (HC<span class=hs> </span>Q) vs. 54.2% (control) which may significantly affect results due to the much higher risk for male patients.<div class=sspace></div>Authors note: &quot;our aim was to exclude patients already receiving longer and potentially therapeutic doses of the study treatments&quot; in explanation for why the study protocol was changed to exclude patients with previous use of the medications >24hrs. Analyzing these patients rather than excluding them may have revealed effectiveness with early use as shown in other studies.<div class=sspace></div>The trial initially required enrollment within 48 hours of admission and was changed to remove this requirement, this change is likely to reduce effectiveness because enrollment was moved later, compared to the time the disease became serious enough for hospitalization.
</td>
</tr>

<td rowspan=5 class="xatd xresult resultpos"><div class=desktop>Positive

<td colspan=3 class="xatd xstage"><div class=desktop>Late treatment study
<span class=ul>&nbsp; <a target=_blank href='https://www.medrxiv.org/content/10.1101/2020.07.17.20155960v1'>Source</a>
 &nbsp; <a href='bernaola.html'>Study Page</a></span>
</div><div class=mobile>Late treatment study</div></td>
</tr>

<tr id=x4b class="xctr xlate  hidden">
<td class="xctd xref" colspan=3><span class=author>Bernaola</span> et al., medRxiv, doi:10.1101/2020.07.17.20155960 (Preprint)</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x4c class="xctr xlate  hidden">
<td class="xctd xtitle" colspan=3>Observational Study of the Efficiency of Treatments in Patients Hospitalized with Covid-19 in Madrid</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x4d class="xctr xlate  hidden">
<td class="xctd xsummary" colspan=3>HC<span class=hs> </span>Q HR 0.83 [0.77-0.89] based on propensity score matched retrospective analysis of 1,645 hospitalized patients. Prednisone HR 0.85 [0.82-0.88], 14 other medications showed either no signicant benefit or a negative effect.
</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x6c class="xctr xpep  hidden">
<td class="xctd xtitle" colspan=3>Efficacy of Hydroxych<span class=hs> </span>loroquine as Prophylaxis for Covid-19</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x6d class="xctr xpep  hidden">
<td class="xctd xsummary" colspan=3>Secondary analysis of Boulware et al.'s PEP trial and treatment delay-response data, confirming that HC<span class=hs> </span>Q is effective when used early, p<0.01.<div class=sspace></div>The effectiveness found is especially notable considering the limitations of the study. Treatment was relatively late, with enrollment up to
4 days after exposure, and an unspecified shipping delay. While the paper does not provide shipping details, the study protocol gives some detail allowing us to estimate the treatment delay as ~70 to 140 hours after exposure on average for the 1-4 days since enrollment specified in the paper (we will update this when authors respond to our request for details). There was only 75% medication adherence, including 16% who did not take the medication at all. The study relies on Internet surveys.
Meta studies are not included in the percentages or study count.
</td>
</tr>

<tr id=r7 class="ratr early ">
<td rowspan=2 class="ratd date"><div class=rotate><div class=rotate2>7/16</div></div></td>
<td rowspan=2 class="ratd result resultinc"><div class=desktop>Inconc.
</div><div id=rm7 class="mobile resultmob"><div class=resultmob2>INCONC.</div></div></td>
<td class="ratd stage">Early</td>
<td class="ratd ref"><span class=author>Skipper</span> et al., Annals of Internal Medicine, doi:10.7326/M20-4207 (Peer Reviewed)</td>
<td class="ratd title">Hydroxych<span class=hs> </span>loroquine in Nonhospitalized Adults With Early COVID-19: A Randomized Trial</td>
</tr>

<tr id=r7b class="rbtr early ">
<td class="rbtd summary" colspan=3>~70 to 140 hour (inc. shipping) delayed outpatient treatment with HC<span class=hs> </span>Q reduced combined hospitalization/death by 50%, p=0.29 (5 HC<span class=hs> </span>Q cases, 10 control cases), and reduced hospitalization by 60%,..</td>
</tr>


<tr id=x7 class="xatr xearly  hidden">
<td rowspan=5 class="xatd date"><div class=rotate><div class=rotate2>7/16</div></div></td>
<td rowspan=5 class="xatd xresult resultinc"><div class=desktop>Inconc.
</div><div id=rm7 class="mobile resultmob"><div class=resultmob2>INCONC.</div></div></td>

<td colspan=3 class="xatd xstage"><div class=desktop>Early treatment study
<span class=ul>&nbsp; <a target=_blank href='https://www.acpjournals.org/doi/10.7326/M20-4207'>Source</a>
 &nbsp; <a href='skipper.html'>Study Page</a></span>
</div><div class=mobile>Early treatment study</div></td>
</tr>

<tr id=x7b class="xctr xearly  hidden">
<td class="xctd xref" colspan=3><span class=author>Skipper</span> et al., Annals of Internal Medicine, doi:10.7326/M20-4207 (Peer Reviewed)</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x7c class="xctr xearly  hidden">
<td class="xctd xtitle" colspan=3>Hydroxych<span class=hs> </span>loroquine in Nonhospitalized Adults With Early COVID-19: A Randomized Trial</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x7d class="xctr xearly  hidden">
<td class="xctd xsummary" colspan=3>~70 to 140 hour (inc. shipping) delayed outpatient treatment with HC<span class=hs> </span>Q reduced combined hospitalization/death by 50%, p=0.29 (5 HC<span class=hs> </span>Q cases, 10 control cases), and reduced hospitalization by 60%, p=0.17. There was one hospitalized control death and one non-hospitalized HC<span class=hs> </span>Q death. It is unclear why there was a non-hospitalized death, external factors such as lack of standard care may be involved. Excluding that case results in one control death and zero HC<span class=hs> </span>Q deaths (not statistically significant but noted as reducing mortality is the most important outcome). Details for the hospitalizations and deaths such as medication adherence and treatment delay may be informative but are not provided.<div class=sspace></div>The paper states the end point was changed from hospitalization/death to symptom severity because they would have required 6,000 participants. However, if the observed trend continued, they would hit 95% significance on the reduction in hospitalization at ~725 patients, and 95% on the reduction in combined hospitalization/death at ~1,145 patients, which is a lot less than 6,000, and also less than the original plan of 1,242 patients. We hope the trial can be continued for statistical significance.<div class=sspace></div>Treatment is relatively late, ~70 to 140 hours after symptoms, including the shipping delay. The paper does not mention the shipping delay but partial details are provided in the study protocol. They are not clear but indicate no shipping on the weekends and a possible 12pm cutoff for same day dispensing and mailing. Assuming that enrollments were evenly distributed between 6am and 12am each day, we get an average of ~46 hours shipping delay. We have asked for shipping details and will update with more accurate values when available. In any case the treatment delay is quite long and there is no overlap with the more typical delays used such as 0 - 36 hours for oseltamivir.<div class=sspace></div>The paper compares 0 - 36 hour delayed treatment with oseltamivir (influenza) and ~70 to 140 hour delayed treatment with HC<span class=hs> </span>Q (COVID-19), noting that oseltamivir seemed more effective. However, a more comparable study is McLean (2015) who showed that 48 - 119 hour delayed treatment with oseltamivir has no effect. This suggests that HC<span class=hs> </span>Q is more effective than oseltamivir, and that HC<span class=hs> </span>Q may still have significant effect for some amount of delay beyond the delay where oseltamivir is effective.<div class=sspace></div>6 people were included that enrolled with >4d symptoms, although they do not match the study inclusion criteria. This reduces observed effectiveness. The paper says 56% (236) were enrolled within 1 day of symptoms, but results show only 40% for &quot;<1d&quot;, 56% is possibly for <48hrs, we have asked for clarification.<div class=sspace></div>Patients in this study are relatively young and most of them recover without assistance. This reduces the room for a treatment to make improvements. The maximum improvement of an effective treatment would be expected before all patients approach recovery, as shown in the figure below. Authors focus on the end result where most have recovered, but it is more informative to examine the curve and the point of maximum effectiveness. Authors did not collect data for every day but they do have interim results for days 3, 5, 10. The results are consistent with an effective treatment and show a statistically significant improvement, p = 0.05, at day 10 (other unreported days might show increased effectiveness).<div class=sspace></div>Results also show a larger treatment effect for those >50, not statistically significant due to the small sample, but noted as COVID-19 risk dramatically increases with age. The effect may be more visible here because younger patients may on average have more mild cases with less room for improvement. In general patients in this study have relatively mild symptoms on average, limiting the chance to observe improvement.<div class=sspace></div>The study relies on Internet surveys. Known fake surveys were submitted to the similar PEP trial and there could be an unknown number of undetected fake surveys in both trials. The study shows a high incidence of side effects in the placebo arm, which could be in part due to fake entries [1].<div class=sspace></div>The granularity change in the histograms of Figure S4 raise concerns [2]. Data on increasing severity, less affected by the lower bound where everyone has recovered, also supports effectiveness [3].<div class=sspace></div>Research shows the placebo used in the US may be protective for COVID-19 [4] so the true effectiveness of HC<span class=hs> </span>Q could be higher than observed.<div class=sspace></div>Treatment delay reporting has changed from the companion PEP trial which reported results for enrollment delays 1, 2, 3, and 4 separately (and from which we can confirm a statistically significant delay-response relationship), while this trial combines 1-2 and 3-4, and adds <1. Since the two trials share reporting (some patients were moved between trials) it's not clear how the new category was added.<div class=sspace></div>RCT of 423 patients with Internet surveys. Medication adherence was only 77% so the true effect of treatment is likely higher. Analysis of primarily low risk patients, authors note the results are not generalizable to the COVID high-risk population. We will update when hearing back on questions asked.<div class=sspace></div>In summary, we believe the results of this study are positive for HC<span class=hs> </span>Q being an effective treatment, however we have classified this study as inconclusive for now pending feedback and further analysis.

<div class=footnote><a target="_blank" href="https://twitter.com/Covid19Crusher/status/1284515906375356416">[2] twitter.com/Covid19Crusher/status/1284515906375356416</a></div>
<div class=footnote><a target="_blank" href="https://twitter.com/Covid19Crusher/status/1284515906375356416">[3] twitter.com/Covid19Crusher/status/1284515906375356416</a></div>

</td>
</tr>

<tr id=r8 class="ratr early ">
<td rowspan=2 class="ratd date"><div class=rotate><div class=rotate2>7/16</div></div></td>
<td rowspan=2 class="ratd result resultinc"><div class=desktop>Inconc.
</div><div id=rm8 class="mobile resultmob"><div class=resultmob2>INCONC.</div></div></td>
<td class="ratd stage">Early</td>
<td class="ratd ref"><span class=author>Mitjà</span> et al., Clinical Infectious Diseases, ciaa1009, doi:10.1093/cid/ciaa1009 (Peer Reviewed)</td>
<td class="ratd title">Hydroxych<span class=hs> </span>loroquine for Early Treatment of Adults with Mild Covid-19: A Randomized-Controlled Trial</td>
</tr>

<tr id=r8b class="rbtr early ">
<td class="rbtd summary" colspan=3>This paper has inconsistent data - some of the values reported in Table 2 and the abstract correspond to 12 control hospitalizations, while others correspond to 11 control hospitalizations.

There was a 25% reduction in hospitalization an..</td>
</tr>


<tr id=x8 class="xatr xearly  hidden">
<td rowspan=5 class="xatd date"><div class=rotate><div class=rotate2>7/16</div></div></td>
<td rowspan=5 class="xatd xresult resultinc"><div class=desktop>Inconc.
</div><div id=rm8 class="mobile resultmob"><div class=resultmob2>INCONC.</div></div></td>

<td colspan=3 class="xatd xstage"><div class=desktop>Early treatment study
<span class=ul>&nbsp; <a target=_blank href='https://academic.oup.com/cid/article/doi/10.1093/cid/ciaa1009/5872589#.XxCYlMdGoJM.twitter'>Source</a>
 &nbsp; <a href='mitja.html'>Study Page</a></span>
</div><div class=mobile>Early treatment study</div></td>
</tr>

<tr id=x8b class="xctr xearly  hidden">
<td class="xctd xref" colspan=3><span class=author>Mitjà</span> et al., Clinical Infectious Diseases, ciaa1009, doi:10.1093/cid/ciaa1009 (Peer Reviewed)</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x8c class="xctr xearly  hidden">
<td class="xctd xtitle" colspan=3>Hydroxych<span class=hs> </span>loroquine for Early Treatment of Adults with Mild Covid-19: A Randomized-Controlled Trial</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x8d class="xctr xearly  hidden">
<td class="xctd xsummary" colspan=3>This paper has inconsistent data - some of the values reported in Table 2 and the abstract correspond to 12 control hospitalizations, while others correspond to 11 control hospitalizations.<div class=sspace></div>There was a 25% reduction in hospitalization and 16% reduction in the median time to symptom resolution for HC<span class=hs> </span>Q, without statistical significance due to small samples.<div class=sspace></div>Treatment delay is unknown at this time. They report a delay of up to 120 hours after symptoms plus an additional unspecified delay where medication was provided to patients at the first home visit. We have asked for details of the treatment delay and will update when hearing back. They do not break down results by treatment delay.<div class=sspace></div>The paper does not mention zinc. Zinc deficiency in Spain has been reported at 83% [1], this may significantly reduce effectiveness. HC<span class=hs> </span>Q is a zinc ionophore which increases cellular uptake, facilitating significant intracellular concentrations of zinc, and zinc is known to inhibit SARS-CoV RNA-dependent RNA polymerase activity, and is widely thought to be important for effectiveness with SARS-CoV-2 [2].<div class=sspace></div>Undetectable viral load was changed to 3 log10 copies/mL potentially masking effectiveness. For viral load authors use nasopharyngeal swabs, we note that viral activity in the lung may be especially important for COVID-19, and that research has shown HC<span class=hs> </span>Q concentrations can be much higher in the lung compared to plasma [3]. We also note that viral detection by PCR does not equate to viable virus [4]. Accuracy of the tests is not provided.<div class=sspace></div>293 low-risk patients with no deaths. No serious adverse events. We have asked for more details on the treatment delay and viral load change and will update when hearing back.
<div class=footnotes><div class=footnote><a target="_blank" href="https://www.mdpi.com/2072-6643/9/7/697">[1] mdpi.com/2072-6643/9/7/697</a></div>
<div class=footnote><a target="_blank" href="https://www.infezmed.it/index.php/article?Anno=2020&numero=2&ArticoloDaVisualizzare=Vol_28_2_2020_192">[2] infezmed.it/index.php/article?Anno=2020&numero=2&ArticoloDaVisualizzare=Vol_28_2_2020_192</a></div>
<div class=footnote><a target="_blank" href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC7122276/HCQ">[3] ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC7122276/HCQ</a></div>
<div class=footnote><a target="_blank" href="https://www.ams.edu.sg/view-pdf.aspx?file=media%5c5556_fi_331.pdf&ofile=Period+of+Infectivity+Position+Statement+(final)+23-5-20+(logos).pdf">[4] ams.edu.sg/view-pdf.aspx?file=media%5c5556_fi_331.pdf&ofile=Period+of+Infectivity+Position+Stateme..</a></div></div>
</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x10 class="xatr xlate  hidden">

<td rowspan=5 class="xatd xresult resultneg"><div class=desktop>Negative
</div><div id=rm10 class="mobile resultmob"><div class=resultmob2>NEGATIVE</div></div></td>

<td colspan=3 class="xatd xstage"><div class=desktop>Late treatment study
<span class=ul>&nbsp; <a target=_blank href='https://www.medrxiv.org/content/10.1101/2020.07.04.20146548v1'>Source</a>
 &nbsp; <a href='an.html'>Study Page</a></span>
</div><div class=mobile>Late treatment study</div></td>
</tr>

<tr id=x10b class="xctr xlate  hidden">
<td class="xctd xref" colspan=3><span class=author>An</span> et al., medRxiv, doi:10.1101/2020.07.04.20146548 (Preprint)</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x10c class="xctr xlate  hidden">
<td class="xctd xtitle" colspan=3>Treatment Response to Hydroxych<span class=hs> </span>loroquine and Antibiotics for mild to moderate COVID-19: a retrospective cohort study from South Korea</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x10d class="xctr xlate  hidden">
<td class="xctd xsummary" colspan=3>Retrospective of hospitalized patients with 31 HC<span class=hs> </span>Q patients and 195 standard treatment patients, not showing a significant difference in terms of viral clearance or recovery. There was no mortality in either group.<div class=sspace></div>&quot;It is notable that HQ plus antibiotics group had worse baseline clinical profiles (i.e. higher percentage of moderate severity patients, more patients with fever >=37.5C, higher average body temperature) and prognostic indicators such as age, LDH, lymphocyte count, and CRP&quot;. <div class=sspace></div>We note that propensity score matching removed almost all of the male patients in the control group (40% -> 5%) but increased the percentage of male patients in the treatment group. This provides a large advantage to the control group because there is a very large difference in severity and mortality based on gender [1].<div class=sspace></div>In terms of viral RNA clearance we note that other research has found that &quot;active viral replication drops quickly after the first week, and viable virus was not found after the second week of illness despite the persistence of PCR detection of RNA” [2].
<div class=footnotes><div class=footnote><a target="_blank" href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC7247289/">[1] ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC7247289/</a></div>
<div class=footnote><a target="_blank" href="https://www.ams.edu.sg/view-pdf.aspx?file=media%5c5556_fi_331.pdf&ofile=Period+of+Infectivity+Position+Statement+(final)+23-5-20+(logos).pdf">[2] ams.edu.sg/view-pdf.aspx?file=media%5c5556_fi_331.pdf&ofile=Period+of+Infectivity+Position+Stateme..</a></div></div>
</td>
</tr>

<td class="xctd xtitle" colspan=3>Treatment with Hydroxych<span class=hs> </span>loroquine, Azithromycin, and Combination in Patients Hospitalized with COVID-19</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x13d class="xctr xlate  hidden">
<td class="xctd xsummary" colspan=3>HC<span class=hs> </span>Q decreases mortality from 26.4% to 13.5% (HC<span class=hs> </span>Q) or 20.1% (HC<span class=hs> </span>Q+AZ). Propensity matched HC<span class=hs> </span>Q HR 0.487, p=0.009. Michigan 2,541 patients retrospective. Before propensity matching the HC<span class=hs> </span>Q group average age is 5 years younger and the percentage of male patients is 4% higher which is likely to favor the treatment and the control respectively in the before-propensity matching results.
<br><br><img data-src=/simg/arshad.png class=simage>
</td>
</tr>

<td class="ratd title">Incidence of arrhythmias and electrocardiographic abnormalities in symptomatic pediatric patients with PCR positive SARS-CoV-2 infection including drug induced changes in the corrected QT interval (QTc)</td>

<tr id=x14 class="xatr xna hidden">
<td rowspan=5 class="xatd date"><div class=rotate><div class=rotate2>7/1</div></div></td>
<td rowspan=5 class="xatd xresult resultneu"><div class=desktop>Safety
</div><div id=rm14 class="mobile resultmob"><div class=resultmob2>SAFETY</div></div></td>

<td colspan=3 class="xatd xstage"><div class=desktop>N/A
<span class=ul>&nbsp; <a target=_blank href='https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC7328618/'>Source</a>
 &nbsp; <a href='samuel.html'>Study Page</a></span>
</div><div class=mobile>N/A</div></td>
</tr>

<tr id=x14b class="xctr xna hidden">
<td class="xctd xref" colspan=3><span class=author>Samuel</span> et al., Heart Rhythm, doi:10.1016/j.hrthm.2020.06.033 (Peer Reviewed) (not included in the study count)</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x14c class="xctr xna hidden">
<td class="xctd xtitle" colspan=3>Incidence of arrhythmias and electrocardiographic abnormalities in symptomatic pediatric patients with PCR positive SARS-CoV-2 infection including drug induced changes in the corrected QT interval (QTc)</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x14d class="xctr xna hidden">
<td class="xctd xsummary" colspan=3>In pediatric patients with PCR positive active COVID-19 infection, significant arrhythmias are infrequent, but occur at an incidence higher than expected in a general pediatric population. Comorbidities are not more common in patients with arrhythmias than in patients without arrhythmias. However, providers still need to be vigilant for comorbidities that may independently place patients at risk for arrhythmias. COVID-19 treatment using HC<span class=hs> </span>Q leads to significant QTc prolongation, but was not associated with arrhythmias in pediatric patients. The long term sequelae of arrhythmia development in this population and their impact on outcome needs to be studied.
</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x16c class="xctr xprep  hidden">
<td class="xctd xtitle" colspan=3>Chronic treatment with hydroxych<span class=hs> </span>loroquine and SARS-CoV-2 infection</td>

<tr id=x16d class="xctr xprep  hidden">
<td class="xctd xsummary" colspan=3>Chronic treatment with HC<span class=hs> </span>Q provides protection against COVID, odds ratio 0.51 (0.37-0.70). Note that patients with SLE, RA, and other autoimmune conditions have a significantly increased susceptibility to and incidence of infections, so the actual benefit may be significantly higher [1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7].

<tr id=r23 class="ratr late ">
<td rowspan=2 class="ratd date"><div class=rotate><div class=rotate2>6/19</div></div></td>
<td rowspan=2 class="ratd result resultpos"><div class=desktop>Positive
</div><div id=rm23 class="mobile resultmob"><div class=resultmob2>POSITIVE</div></div></td>
<td class="ratd stage">Late</td>
<td class="ratd ref"><span class=author>Sbidian</span> et al., medRxiv, doi:10.1101/2020.06.16.20132597 (Preprint)</td>
<td class="ratd title">Hydroxych<span class=hs> </span>loroquine with or without azithromycin and in-hospital mortality or discharge in patients hospitalized for COVID-19 infection: a cohort study of 4,642 in-patients in France</td>
</tr>

<tr id=r23b class="rbtr late ">
<td class="rbtd summary" colspan=3>Retrospective of 4,642 hospitalized patients in France showing significantly faster discharge with HC<span class=hs> </span>Q and HC<span class=hs> </span>Q+AZ. No significant effect is seen on 28-day mortality, however many more control ..</td>
</tr>


<tr id=x23 class="xatr xlate  hidden">
<td rowspan=5 class="xatd date"><div class=rotate><div class=rotate2>6/19</div></div></td>
<td rowspan=5 class="xatd xresult resultpos"><div class=desktop>Positive
</div><div id=rm23 class="mobile resultmob"><div class=resultmob2>POSITIVE</div></div></td>

<td colspan=3 class="xatd xstage"><div class=desktop>Late treatment study
<span class=ul>&nbsp; <a target=_blank href='https://www.medrxiv.org/content/10.1101/2020.06.16.20132597v1'>Source</a>
 &nbsp; <a href='sbidian.html'>Study Page</a></span>
</div><div class=mobile>Late treatment study</div></td>
</tr>

<tr id=x23b class="xctr xlate  hidden">
<td class="xctd xref" colspan=3><span class=author>Sbidian</span> et al., medRxiv, doi:10.1101/2020.06.16.20132597 (Preprint)</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x23c class="xctr xlate  hidden">
<td class="xctd xtitle" colspan=3>Hydroxych<span class=hs> </span>loroquine with or without azithromycin and in-hospital mortality or discharge in patients hospitalized for COVID-19 infection: a cohort study of 4,642 in-patients in France</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x23d class="xctr xlate  hidden">
<td class="xctd xsummary" colspan=3>Retrospective of 4,642 hospitalized patients in France showing significantly faster discharge with HC<span class=hs> </span>Q and HC<span class=hs> </span>Q+AZ. No significant effect is seen on 28-day mortality, however many more control patients are still in hospital at 28 days suggesting there will be a significant improvement when extending past 28 days. Note that the median age is higher in the group not treated with HC<span class=hs> </span>Q or AZ. For other issues with the adjustments see [1]. Also see the analysis here [2]. We received feedback from one person that thinks the trial should be considered negative because the control patients still in hospital should be disregarded. However, based on other studies, it seems very likely that a significant number of deaths in the control group occurred past 28 days whereas no treated patients remained in hospital. This should be simple for the authors to resolve by extending the analysis. Even if we ignore this, it still shows significantly faster discharge for treatment, so we do not see how we can consider it negative. We note that the substantial reduction in hospital time is a very large cost reduction and may lower mortality in general by reducing the chance of exceeding maximum capacity. Additional feedback is welcome.
<br><br><img data-src=/simg/sbidian.png class=simage>
<div class=footnotes><div class=footnote><a target="_blank" href="https://www.medrxiv.org/content/10.1101/2020.06.16.20132597v1#disqus_thread">[1] medrxiv.org/content/10.1101/2020.06.16.20132597v1#disqus_thread</a></div>
<div class=footnote><a target="_blank" href="https://twitter.com/Covid19Crusher/status/1274668697408471040">[2] twitter.com/Covid19Crusher/status/1274668697408471040</a></div></div>
</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x23e class="xbtr xlate  hidden">
<td class="xbtd xurl" colspan=3>

<a href='sbidian.html'>Study Page</a> &nbsp;
<a target=_blank href='https://www.facebook.com/sharer/sharer.php?u=https%3A%2F%2Fc19study.com%2Fsbidian.html'><span class=tweets><img class='tweetimg fbimg' src='fb.svg'></span></a>

<tr id=r24 class="ratr late ">
<td rowspan=2 class="ratd date"><div class=rotate><div class=rotate2>6/18</div></div></td>
<td rowspan=2 class="ratd result resultinc"><div class=desktop>Inconc.
</div><div id=rm24 class="mobile resultmob"><div class=resultmob2>INCONC.</div></div></td>
<td class="ratd stage">Late</td>
<td class="ratd ref"><span class=author>Paccoud</span> et al., Clinical Infectious Diseases, doi:10.1093/cid/ciaa791 (Peer Reviewed)</td>
<td class="ratd title">Compassionate use of hydroxych<span class=hs> </span>loroquine in clinical practice for patients with mild to severe Covid-19 in a French university hospital</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x29c class="xctr xlate  hidden">
<td class="xctd xtitle" colspan=3>Early administration of lopinavir/ritonavir plus hydroxych<span class=hs> </span>loroquine does not alter the clinical course of SARS-CoV-2 infection: a retrospective cohort study</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x29d class="xctr xlate  hidden">
<td class="xctd xsummary" colspan=3>Late stage study of hospitalized patients comparing treatment starting within 5 days versus later. Note that &quot;early&quot; here is only relative - all patients are hospitalized so this is &quot;late&quot; and &quot;very late&quot;. The &quot;early&quot; treatment group is significantly older. Severe adverse events attributed by authors to concurrent administration of LPV, making it difficult to make conclusions about HC<span class=hs> </span>Q.
</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x35c class="xctr xpep  hidden">
<td class="xctd xtitle" colspan=3>A Randomized Trial of Hydroxych<span class=hs> </span>loroquine as Postexposure Prophylaxis for Covid-19</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x35d class="xctr xpep  hidden">
<td class="xctd xsummary" colspan=3>COVID-19 cases are reduced by [49%, 29%, 16%] respectively when taken within ~[70, 94, 118] hours of exposure (including shipping delay). The treatment delay-response relationship is significant at p=0.002. PEP delayed treatment RCT.<div class=sspace></div>Currently this is the only study where we have evaluated the result as positive while the authors indicate it is negative. We provide a <a href='/boulware.html'>detailed explanation of why the results presented here are positive</a> [1]. Note that author comments also differ from the published conclusion.

<tr id=x42c class="xctr xlate  hidden">
<td class="xctd xtitle" colspan=3>Hydroxych<span class=hs> </span>loroquine and Tocilizumab Therapy in COVID-19 Patients - An Observational Study</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x42d class="xctr xlate  hidden">
<td class="xctd xsummary" colspan=3>Retrospective study of late stage use on 2,512 hospitalized patients showing no significant differences in associated mortality for patients receiving any HC<span class=hs> </span>Q during the hospitalization (HR, 0.99 [95% CI, 0.80-1.22]), HC<span class=hs> </span>Q alone (HR, 1.02 [95% CI, 0.83-1.27]), or HC<span class=hs> </span>Q+AZ (HR, 0.98 [95% CI, 0.75-1.28]). Misclassification is possible due to manual abstraction of EHR data. They observed a change in the prescribing patterns of HC<span class=hs> </span>Q during the study timeframe. Confounding by indication.
</td>
</tr>

</tr>

<tr id=x46c class="xctr xlate  hidden">
<td class="xctd xtitle" colspan=3>Outcomes of Hydroxych<span class=hs> </span>loroquine Treatment Among Hospitalized COVID-19 Patients in the United States- Real-World Evidence From a Federated Electronic Medical Record Network</td>

<tr id=x46d class="xctr xlate  hidden">
<td class="xctd xsummary" colspan=3>EHR analysis of 3,372 hospitalized COVID-19 patients not showing a significant difference for mortality or the risk of mechanical ventilation. Subject to the limitations of EHR analysis. Misclassification is possible. Confounding by indication.

<tr id=x49 class="xatr xprep  hidden">
<td rowspan=5 class="xatd date"><div class=rotate><div class=rotate2>5/16</div></div></td>
<td rowspan=5 class="xatd xresult resultinc"><div class=desktop>Inconc.
</div><div id=rm49 class="mobile resultmob"><div class=resultmob2>INCONC.</div></div></td>

<td colspan=3 class="xatd xstage"><div class=desktop>Pre-Exposure Prophylaxis study
<span class=ul>&nbsp; <a target=_blank href='https://www.medrxiv.org/content/10.1101/2020.05.16.20104141v1.full.pdf'>Source</a>
 &nbsp; <a href='macias.html'>Study Page</a></span>
</div><div class=mobile>Pre-Exposure Prophylaxis study</div></td>
</tr>

<tr id=x49b class="xctr xprep  hidden">
<td class="xctd xref" colspan=3><span class=author>Macias</span> et al., medRxiv, 10.1101/2020.05.16.20104141 (Preprint)</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x49c class="xctr xprep  hidden">
<td class="xctd xtitle" colspan=3>Similar incidence of Coronavirus Disease 2019 (COVID-19) in patients with rheumatic diseases with and without hydroxych<span class=hs> </span>loroquine therapy</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x49d class="xctr xprep  hidden">
<td class="xctd xsummary" colspan=3>Very small retrospective study of rheumatic disease patients, sample size is too small for statistical significance (HC<span class=hs> </span>Q 0.5-4.0%, no-HC<span class=hs> </span>Q 0.4-2.7%). Confirmed cases were 1 HC<span class=hs> </span>Q and 2 no-HC<span class=hs> </span>Q, confimed+likely cases were 1 HC<span class=hs> </span>Q and 3 no-HC<span class=hs> </span>Q. 1 HC<span class=hs> </span>Q and 2 no-HC<span class=hs> </span>Q patients were admitted to hospital. We do not think a conclusion can be drawn based on these sample sizes. Further, there are very significant differences between the groups, for example 30% of the HC<span class=hs> </span>Q group have SLE vs. 2.5% of the no-HC<span class=hs> </span>Q group. SLE patients have a 5.7 times relative risk of pneumonia according to [1], whereas the relative risk with glucocorticoids and TNF-α inhibitors is significantly lower [2]. Two more recent studies with rheumatic disease/autoimmune condition patients provide higher confidence.
<div class=footnotes><div class=footnote><a target="_blank" href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC4516647/">[1] ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC4516647/</a></div>
<div class=footnote><a target="_blank" href="https://academic.oup.com/rheumatology/article/52/1/53/1830871">[2] academic.oup.com/rheumatology/article/52/1/53/1830871</a></div></div>
</td>
</tr>

<td class="ratd stage">Late</td>
<td class="ratd ref"><span class=author>Geleris</span> et al., NEJM, May 7, 2020, doi:10.1056/NEJMoa2012410 (Peer Reviewed)</td>
<td class="ratd title">Observational Study of Hydroxych<span class=hs> </span>loroquine in Hospitalized Patients with Covid-19</td>
</tr>

<tr id=r57b class="rbtr late ">
<td class="rbtd summary" colspan=3>There appears to be a major error in this paper. Before propensity matching, 38 control patients had hypertension. After propensity matching, 146 patients had hypertension (Table 1). This is not possible. Even if all propensity matched co..</td>
</tr>


<tr id=x57 class="xatr xlate  hidden">
<td rowspan=5 class="xatd date"><div class=rotate><div class=rotate2>5/7</div></div></td>
<td rowspan=5 class="xatd xresult resultinc"><div class=desktop>Inconc.
</div><div id=rm57 class="mobile resultmob"><div class=resultmob2>INCONC.</div></div></td>

<td colspan=3 class="xatd xstage"><div class=desktop>Late treatment study
<span class=ul>&nbsp; <a target=_blank href='https://www.nejm.org/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMoa2012410'>Source</a>
 &nbsp; <a href='geleris.html'>Study Page</a></span>
</div><div class=mobile>Late treatment study</div></td>
</tr>

<tr id=x57b class="xctr xlate  hidden">
<td class="xctd xref" colspan=3><span class=author>Geleris</span> et al., NEJM, May 7, 2020, doi:10.1056/NEJMoa2012410 (Peer Reviewed)</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x57c class="xctr xlate  hidden">
<td class="xctd xtitle" colspan=3>Observational Study of Hydroxych<span class=hs> </span>loroquine in Hospitalized Patients with Covid-19</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x57d class="xctr xlate  hidden">
<td class="xctd xsummary" colspan=3>There appears to be a major error in this paper. Before propensity matching, 38 control patients had hypertension. After propensity matching, 146 patients had hypertension (Table 1). This is not possible. Even if all propensity matched control patients had hypertension, the control prevalence would only be 14% compared to 49% for treatment. Since patients with hypertension are at much greater risk of mortality (HR 2.12, see [1]), this appears to invalidate the results.<div class=sspace></div>Observational study of 1,446 hospitalized patients showing no significant effect on a combined intubation/death outcome for late treatment.<div class=sspace></div>However, secondary analysis shows the success of HC<span class=hs> </span>Q was hidden by combining intubation and death - death / (combined death/intubation) for HC<span class=hs> </span>Q was 60% vs. control 89%, for details see: [2].<div class=sspace></div>RCT recommended. No AZ or Zinc. HC<span class=hs> </span>Q group much sicker - patients already in mild/moderate ARDS, most of the control group not in ARDS. Control cases received other therapeutics.
<br><br><img data-src=/simg/geleris.png class=simage>
<div class=footnotes><div class=footnote><a target="_blank" href="https://academic.oup.com/eurheartj/article/41/22/2058/5851436">[1] academic.oup.com/eurheartj/article/41/22/2058/5851436</a></div>
<div class=footnote><a target="_blank" href="https://twitter.com/dperetti/status/1259154540630364162">[2] twitter.com/dperetti/status/1259154540630364162</a></div></div>
</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x57e class="xbtr xlate  hidden">

<td class="ratd stage">Animal</td>
<td class="ratd ref"><span class=author>Maisonnasse</span> et al., Nature, 2020, doi:10.1038/s41586-020-2558-4 (preprint 5/6) (Peer Reviewed) (not included in the study count)</td>
<td class="ratd title">Hydroxych<span class=hs> </span>loroquine use against SARS-CoV-2 infection in non-human primates</td>
</tr>

<tr id=r59b class="rbtr na">
<td class="rbtd summary" colspan=3>Monkey study which reports no effect of HC<span class=hs> </span>Q or HC<span class=hs> </span>Q+AZ. However, there are actually several signs of effectiveness despite the very small sample sizes and 100% recovery of all treated and contr..</td>
</tr>


<tr id=x59 class="xatr xna hidden">
<td rowspan=5 class="xatd date"><div class=rotate><div class=rotate2>5/6</div></div></td>
<td rowspan=5 class="xatd xresult resultneu"><div class=desktop>Animal
</div><div id=rm59 class="mobile resultmob"><div class=resultmob2>ANIMAL</div></div></td>

<td colspan=3 class="xatd xstage"><div class=desktop>Animal study
<span class=ul>&nbsp; <a target=_blank href='https://www.nature.com/articles/s41586-020-2558-4_reference.pdf'>Source</a>
 &nbsp; <a href='maisonnasse.html'>Study Page</a></span>
</div><div class=mobile>Animal study</div></td>
</tr>

<tr id=x59b class="xctr xna hidden">
<td class="xctd xref" colspan=3><span class=author>Maisonnasse</span> et al., Nature, 2020, doi:10.1038/s41586-020-2558-4 (preprint 5/6) (Peer Reviewed) (not included in the study count)</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x59c class="xctr xna hidden">
<td class="xctd xtitle" colspan=3>Hydroxych<span class=hs> </span>loroquine use against SARS-CoV-2 infection in non-human primates</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x59d class="xctr xna hidden">
<td class="xctd xsummary" colspan=3>Monkey study which reports no effect of HC<span class=hs> </span>Q or HC<span class=hs> </span>Q+AZ. However, there are actually several signs of effectiveness despite the very small sample sizes and 100% recovery of all treated and control monkeys.<div class=sspace></div>58% reduction in lung lesions: the final day lung lesion data shows 63% of control monkeys have lesions, while 26% of treated monkeys do, p=0.095 (the final day data is missing for 7 monkeys, these are predicted based on the day 5 results and the trend of comparable monkeys).<div class=sspace></div>97% increase in viral load recovery after one week: 3 of 8 control monkeys (38%) have recovered with <= 4 log10 copies/mL viral load, compared to 17 of 23 treated monkeys (74%), p=0.095. 3 of 8 (38%) control monkeys also have a higher peak viral load than 100% of the 23 treated monkeys post-treatment. The group with the lowest peak viral load is the PrEP group.<div class=sspace></div>All animals were infected with the same initial viral load, whereas real-world infections vary in the initial viral load, and lower inital viral loads allow greater time to mount an immune response.
</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x59e class="xbtr xna hidden">
<td class="xbtd xurl" colspan=3>

<td class="ratd ref"><span class=author>Gendelman</span> et al., Autoimmunity Reviews, 19:7, July 2020, doi:10.1016/j.autrev.2020.102566 (Peer Reviewed)</td>
<td class="ratd title">Continuous Hydroxych<span class=hs> </span>loroquine or Colchicine Therapy Does Not Prevent Infection With SARS-CoV-2: Insights From a Large Healthcare Database Analysis</td>
</tr>

<tr id=r62b class="rbtr prep ">
<td class="rbtd summary" colspan=3>Very small study of rheumatic disease/autoimmune disorder patients showing no significant difference but with only 3 chronic HC<span class=hs> </span>Q patient cases. Only considers people tested at a time when primarily symptomatic cases..</td>

<tr id=x62 class="xatr xprep  hidden">
<td rowspan=5 class="xatd date"><div class=rotate><div class=rotate2>5/5</div></div></td>
<td rowspan=5 class="xatd xresult resultinc"><div class=desktop>Inconc.
</div><div id=rm62 class="mobile resultmob"><div class=resultmob2>INCONC.</div></div></td>

<td colspan=3 class="xatd xstage"><div class=desktop>Pre-Exposure Prophylaxis study
<span class=ul>&nbsp; <a target=_blank href='https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S1568997220301282?via%3Dihub'>Source</a>
 &nbsp; <a href='gendelman.html'>Study Page</a></span>
</div><div class=mobile>Pre-Exposure Prophylaxis study</div></td>
</tr>

<tr id=x62b class="xctr xprep  hidden">
<td class="xctd xref" colspan=3><span class=author>Gendelman</span> et al., Autoimmunity Reviews, 19:7, July 2020, doi:10.1016/j.autrev.2020.102566 (Peer Reviewed)</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x62c class="xctr xprep  hidden">
<td class="xctd xtitle" colspan=3>Continuous Hydroxych<span class=hs> </span>loroquine or Colchicine Therapy Does Not Prevent Infection With SARS-CoV-2: Insights From a Large Healthcare Database Analysis</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x62d class="xctr xprep  hidden">
<td class="xctd xsummary" colspan=3>Very small study of rheumatic disease/autoimmune disorder patients showing no significant difference but with only 3 chronic HC<span class=hs> </span>Q patient cases. Only considers people tested at a time when primarily symptomatic cases were tested. Note that patients with SLE, RA, and other autoimmune conditions have a significantly increased susceptibility to and incidence of infections [1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7], with this context the results suggest HC<span class=hs> </span>Q is effective, but this is still inconclusive with the small sample size. Two more recent studies with rheumatic disease/autoimmune condition patients provide higher confidence.
<div class=footnotes><div class=footnote><a target="_blank" href="https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/27370880/">[1] pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/27370880/</a></div>
<div class=footnote><a target="_blank" href="https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/8778988/">[2] pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/8778988/</a></div>
<div class=footnote><a target="_blank" href="https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/23192911/">[3] pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/23192911/</a></div>
<div class=footnote><a target="_blank" href="https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/11447699/">[4] pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/11447699/</a></div>
<div class=footnote><a target="_blank" href="https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/30954968/">[5] pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/30954968/</a></div>
<div class=footnote><a target="_blank" href="https://advancesinrheumatology.biomedcentral.com/articles/10.1186/s42358-019-0055-y">[6] advancesinrheumatology.biomedcentral.com/articles/10.1186/s42358-019-0055-y</a></div>
<div class=footnote><a target="_blank" href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC6099129/">[7] ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC6099129/</a></div></div>
</td>
</tr>

<td class="ratd title">Risk of QT Interval Prolongation Associated With Use of Hydroxych<span class=hs> </span>loroquine With or Without Concomitant Azithromycin Among Hospitalized Patients Testing Positive for Coronavirus Disease 2019 (COVID-19)</td>
</tr>

<tr id=r63b class="rbtr na">
<td class="rbtd summary" colspan=3>Study of 90 hospitalized patients given HC<span class=hs> </span>Q, 53 also receiving AZ, 53% hypertension, 29% diabetes mellitus, baseline median QTc 473ms for HC<span class=hs> </span>Q, and 442ms for HC<span class=hs> </span>Q+AZ. Medi..</td>

<tr id=x63 class="xatr xna hidden">
<td rowspan=5 class="xatd date"><div class=rotate><div class=rotate2>5/1</div></div></td>
<td rowspan=5 class="xatd xresult resultneu"><div class=desktop>Safety
</div><div id=rm63 class="mobile resultmob"><div class=resultmob2>SAFETY</div></div></td>

<td colspan=3 class="xatd xstage"><div class=desktop>N/A
<span class=ul>&nbsp; <a target=_blank href='https://jamanetwork.com/journals/jamacardiology/fullarticle/2765631'>Source</a>
 &nbsp; <a href='mercuro.html'>Study Page</a></span>
</div><div class=mobile>N/A</div></td>
</tr>

<tr id=x63b class="xctr xna hidden">
<td class="xctd xref" colspan=3><span class=author>Mercuro</span> et al., JAMA Cardiol., May 1, 2020, doi:10.1001/jamacardio.2020.1834 (Peer Reviewed) (not included in the study count)</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x63c class="xctr xna hidden">
<td class="xctd xtitle" colspan=3>Risk of QT Interval Prolongation Associated With Use of Hydroxych<span class=hs> </span>loroquine With or Without Concomitant Azithromycin Among Hospitalized Patients Testing Positive for Coronavirus Disease 2019 (COVID-19)</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x63d class="xctr xna hidden">
<td class="xctd xsummary" colspan=3>Study of 90 hospitalized patients given HC<span class=hs> </span>Q, 53 also receiving AZ, 53% hypertension, 29% diabetes mellitus, baseline median QTc 473ms for HC<span class=hs> </span>Q, and 442ms for HC<span class=hs> </span>Q+AZ. Median change for HC<span class=hs> </span>Q+AZ ΔQTc of 23ms vs. 5.5ms for HC<span class=hs> </span>Q. Other factors such as stress cardiomyopathy or myocarditis could not be ruled out. Without a control arm, they could not conclude that HC<span class=hs> </span>Q and AZ conferred increased cardiotoxic risk; however, compared with HC<span class=hs> </span>Q alone, ΔQTc differences were likely associated with the addition of AZ. The likelihood of prolonged QTc was greater in those who received concomitant loop diuretics or had a baseline QTc of 450 milliseconds or more. HC<span class=hs> </span>Q was discontinued in 10 patients due to adverse events including nausea, hypoglycemia, and 1 case of torsades de pointes. There were no deaths reported.<div class=sspace></div>Appropriate use and careful analysis of contraindications, risks, and benefits are important. More recent and much larger studies have not shown significant safety concerns, including outpatient RCTs showing no serious adverse events, and even the RECOVERY trial which used an unusually high dose of HC<span class=hs> </span>Q (including 237 patients also receiving AZ) reports they &quot;did not show any excess in ventricular tachycardia (including torsade de pointes) or ventricular fibrillation in the hydroxych<span class=hs> </span>loroquine arm&quot;, and &quot;serious cardiovascular toxicity has been reported very rarely despite the high prevalence of cardiovascular disease in hospitalized patients, the common occurrence of myocarditis in COVID-19, and the extensive use of hydroxych<span class=hs> </span>loroquine and azithromycin together.&quot;
</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x64 class="xatr xna hidden">
<td rowspan=5 class="xatd date"><div class=rotate><div class=rotate2>5/1</div></div></td>
<td rowspan=5 class="xatd xresult resultneu"><div class=desktop>Safety

<td colspan=3 class="xatd xstage"><div class=desktop>N/A
<span class=ul>&nbsp; <a target=_blank href='https://jamanetwork.com/journals/jamacardiology/fullarticle/2765633'>Source</a>
 &nbsp; <a href='bessiere.html'>Study Page</a></span>
</div><div class=mobile>N/A</div></td>

<tr id=x64b class="xctr xna hidden">
<td class="xctd xref" colspan=3><span class=author>Bessière</span> et al., JAMA Cardiol., May 1, 2020, doi:10.1001/jamacardio.2020.1787 (Peer Reviewed) (not included in the study count)</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x64c class="xctr xna hidden">
<td class="xctd xtitle" colspan=3>Assessment of QT Intervals in a Case Series of Patients With Coronavirus Disease 2019 (COVID-19) Infection Treated With Hydroxych<span class=hs> </span>loroquine Alone or in Combination With Azithromycin in an Intensive Care Unit</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x64d class="xctr xna hidden">
<td class="xctd xsummary" colspan=3>Study of 40 very serious condition ICU patients, 75% required invasive mechanical ventilation, 63% received vasoactive drugs, 50% received other treatments favoring QT prolongation. HC<span class=hs> </span>Q with or w/o AZ was given to 45% and 55% respectively. They showed an increase in QTc, more significant with the combination of HC<span class=hs> </span>Q+AZ where prolonged QTc was observed in 36% (10 with ΔQTc >60 milliseconds and 7 with QTc ≥500 milliseconds). No ventricular arrhythmia, including torsades de pointes, was recorded. While these results may not be generalizable outside the ICU, caution is recommended in use, especially with the combination.<div class=sspace></div>Appropriate use and careful analysis of contraindications, risks, and benefits are important. More recent and much larger studies have not shown significant safety concerns, including outpatient RCTs showing no serious adverse events, and even the RECOVERY trial which used an unusually high dose of HC<span class=hs> </span>Q (including 237 patients also receiving AZ) reports they &quot;did not show any excess in ventricular tachycardia (including torsade de pointes) or ventricular fibrillation in the hydroxych<span class=hs> </span>loroquine arm&quot;, and &quot;serious cardiovascular toxicity has been reported very rarely despite the high prevalence of cardiovascular disease in hospitalized patients, the common occurrence of myocarditis in COVID-19, and the extensive use of hydroxych<span class=hs> </span>loroquine and azithromycin together.&quot;
</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x85c class="xctr xna hidden">
<td class="xctd xtitle" colspan=3>Is Hydroxych<span class=hs> </span>loroquine a Possible Post-Exposure Prophylaxis Drug to Limit the Transmission to Health Care Workers Exposed to COVID19?</td>

<tr id=x89b class="xctr xna hidden">
<td class="xctd xref" colspan=3><span class=author>Liu</span> et al., Cell Discovery 6, 16 (2020), doi:10.1038/s41421-020-0156-0 (Peer Reviewed) (In Vitro) (not included in the study count)</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x89c class="xctr xna hidden">
<td class="xctd xtitle" colspan=3>Hydroxych<span class=hs> </span>loroquine, a less toxic derivative of ch<span class=hs> </span>loroquine, is effective in inhibiting SARS-CoV-2 infection in vitro</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x89d class="xctr xna hidden">
<td class="xctd xsummary" colspan=3>HC<span class=hs> </span>Q effective <i>in vitro</i> and less toxic than C<span class=hs> </span>Q. In addition to direct antiviral activity, HC<span class=hs> </span>Q is a safe and successful anti-inflammatory agent that has been used extensively in autoimmune diseases and can significantly decrease the production of cytokines and, in particular, pro-inflammatory factors. Therefore, in COVID-19 patients, HC<span class=hs> </span>Q may also contribute to attenuating the inflammatory response. Careful design of clinical trials is important to achieve efficient and safe control of the infection.
</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x104 class="xatr xna hidden">
<td rowspan=5 class="xatd date"><div class=rotate><div class=rotate2>2009</div></div></td>
<td rowspan=5 class="xatd xresult resultneu"><div class=desktop>Animal

<td colspan=3 class="xatd xstage"><div class=desktop>Animal study
<span class=ul>&nbsp; <a target=_blank href='https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC2715625/'>Source</a>
 &nbsp; <a href='keyaertsaac.html'>Study Page</a></span>
</div><div class=mobile>Animal study</div></td>
</tr>

<tr id=x104b class="xctr xna hidden">
<td class="xctd xref" colspan=3><span class=author>Keyaerts</span> et al., Antimicrob. Agents Chemother, August 2009, 53(8), doi:0.1128/AAC.01509-08 (Peer Reviewed) (not included in the study count)</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x104c class="xctr xna hidden">
<td class="xctd xtitle" colspan=3>Antiviral Activity of Ch<span class=hs> </span>loroquine against Human Coronavirus OC43 Infection in Newborn Mice</td>
</tr>

<tr id=x104d class="xctr xna hidden">
<td class="xctd xsummary" colspan=3>C<span class=hs> </span>Q inhibits HCoV-OC43 replication in HRT-18 cells. A lethal HCoV-OC43 infection in newborn C57BL/6 mice can be treated with C<span class=hs> </span>Q acquired transplacentally or via maternal milk. The highest survival rate (98.6%) was found when mother mice were treated daily with a concentration of 15 mg of C<span class=hs> </span>Q per kg of body weight. Survival rates declined in a dose-dependent manner, with 88% survival when treated with 5 mg/kg C<span class=hs> </span>Q and 13% survival when treated with 1 mg/kg C<span class=hs> </span>Q. C<span class=hs> </span>Q can be highly effective against HCoV-OC43 infection in newborn mice and may be considered as a future drug against HCoVs.
</td>
</tr>

IC50 for inhibition of SARS-CoV <i>in vitro</i> approximates the plasma concentrations of C<span class=hs> </span>Q reached during treatment of acute malaria. C<span class=hs> </span>Q may be considered for immediate use in the prevention and treatment of SARS-CoV infections.
<br><br><img data-src=/simg/keyaerts.png class=simage>
</td>

function el(s) {
 return document.getElementById(s);

var supportsPassive = false;
try {
  var opts = Object.defineProperty({}, 'passive', {
    get: function() {
      supportsPassive = true;
    }
  });
  window.addEventListener("testPassive", null, opts);
  window.removeEventListener("testPassive", null, opts);
} catch (e) {}
var textarea = document.querySelector('textarea');
textarea.addEventListener('keydown', autosize, supportsPassive ? { passive: true } : false);
textarea.addEventListener('focus', autosize, supportsPassive ? { passive: true } : false);
function autosize() {
  var el = this;
  setTimeout(function() {
    el.style.height='auto';
    el.style.height=(el.scrollHeight + 2)+'px';
    // el.style.cssText = 'height:auto;padding:30px;';  // color:#000
    // el.style.cssText = 'height:' + (el.scrollHeight + 2) + 'px;padding:30px;';
    // for box-sizing other than "content-box" use: el.style.cssText = '-moz-box-sizing:content-box';
    // if (el.value.startsWith('Enter your')) { el.value = ''; el.style.color = '#000000'; }
  }, 0);
}
// document.getElementById('feedback').focus();
var ajax = {};
ajax.x = function() {
  if (typeof XMLHttpRequest !== 'undefined') {
    return new XMLHttpRequest();
  }
  var versions = [ "MSXML2.XmlHttp.6.0","MSXML2.XmlHttp.5.0","MSXML2.XmlHttp.4.0",
    "MSXML2.XmlHttp.3.0","MSXML2.XmlHttp.2.0","Microsoft.XmlHttp" ];
  var xhr;
  for (var i = 0; i < versions.length; i++) {
    try {
      xhr = new ActiveXObject(versions[i]);
      break;
    } catch (e) {
    }
  }
  return xhr;
};
ajax.send = function(url, callback, method, data, async) {
  if (async === undefined) {
    async = true;
  }
  var x = ajax.x();
  x.open(method, url, async);
  x.onreadystatechange = function() {
    if (x.readyState == 4) {
      callback(x.status, x.responseText)
    }
  };
  if (method == 'POST') {
    x.setRequestHeader('Content-type', 'application/x-www-form-urlencoded');
  }
  x.send(data)
};
ajax.get = function(url, data, callback, async) {
  var query = [];
  for (var key in data) {
    query.push(encodeURIComponent(key) + '=' + encodeURIComponent(data[key]));
  }
  ajax.send(url + (query.length ? '?' + query.join('&') : ''), callback, 'GET', null, async)
};
ajax.post = function(url, data, callback, async) {
  var query = [];
  for (var key in data) {
    query.push(encodeURIComponent(key) + '=' + encodeURIComponent(data[key]));
  }
  ajax.send(url, callback, 'POST', query.join('&'), async)
};
var sid = '';
function submit(id) {
  sid = id;
  // console.log('submit ' + sid);
  e = el("feedback");
  // e.scrollIntoView();
  e.focus();
}
function OnSubmit() {
  comment = el("feedback").value;
  if (comment.length > 0) {
    // console.log('sid ' + sid);
    if (sid.length > 0) {
      comment += ' [' + sid + ']';
    }
    el('subresp').innerHTML = "Submitting..";
    ajax.post('/sub', {"comment": comment}, function(code, s) {
      // console.log(code);
      // console.log(s);
      if (code == 200) {
        el('subresp').innerHTML = "Submitted, thanks!"
        // <br><br>You submitted:<br><br>" + comment;
        el("feedback").value = '';
      } else {
        el('subresp').innerHTML = "Error, please try later.<br>";
      }
    });
  } else {
    el('subresp').innerHTML = "Enter some feedback first."
  }
}
function download(id,t) {
  var e = document.getElementById('dl'+id);
  e.style.top = t+'px';
  e.style.display = 'block';
}
function download2(id) {
  var e = document.getElementById('dl'+id);
  e.style.display = 'none';
}
function restrict(n) {
  types = [ 'prep', 'pep', 'early', 'late', 'na' ]
  for (i = 0; i < types.length; i++) {
    if (i == n) {
      document.getElementById('restrict' + i).classList.add('restrictsel');
      document.getElementById('sum' + i).classList.remove('hidden');
    } else {
      document.getElementById('restrict' + i).classList.remove('restrictsel');
      document.getElementById('sum' + i).classList.add('hidden');
    }
    var e = document.getElementsByClassName(types[i]);
    for (j = 0; j < e.length; j++) {
      if (i == n || n == 4) {
        e[j].classList.remove('hidden')
      } else {
        e[j].classList.add('hidden')
      }
    }
    e = document.getElementsByClassName('x' + types[i]);
    for (j = 0; j < e.length; j++) {
      e[j].classList.add('hidden')
    }
  }
  /*
  for (i = 0; i <= n; i++) {
    var e = document.getElementsByClassName(types[i])
    for (j = 0; j < e.length; j++) {
      e[j].classList.remove('hidden')
    }
  }
  for (i = n + 1; i <= types.length; i++) {
    var e = document.getElementsByClassName(types[i])
    for (j = 0; j < e.length; j++) {
      e[j].classList.add('hidden')
    }
  }
  */
}
var current_chart=1;
var max_chart=2;
function next(d) {
  current_chart += d;
  if (current_chart > max_chart) {
    current_chart = 1;
  }
  if (current_chart < 1) {
    current_chart = max_chart;
  }
  setchart(current_chart);
}
var ts = -1;
function tstart(e) {
  ts = e.changedTouches[0].screenX;
  console.log(ts);
}
function tend(e) {
  console.log(e);
  te = e.changedTouches[0].screenX;
  console.log(te);
  if (te > ts + 5) next(-1);
  if (te < ts - 5) next(1);
}
function moveto(d) {
  current_chart = d;
  setchart(d);
}
function setchart(d) {
  for (i = 1; i <= max_chart; i++) {
    e = el('c' + i);
    d = el('dot' + i);

    if (i == current_chart) {
      e.classList.remove('hidden');
      d.classList.add('cdotsel');
    } else {
      e.classList.add('hidden');
      d.classList.remove('cdotsel');
    }
  }
}
if (!Element.prototype.matches) {
  Element.prototype.matches = Element.prototype.msMatchesSelector ||
                              Element.prototype.webkitMatchesSelector;
}
if (!Element.prototype.closest) {
  Element.prototype.closest = function(s) {
    var el = this;
    do {
      if (Element.prototype.matches.call(el, s)) return el;
      el = el.parentElement || el.parentNode;
    } while (el !== null && el.nodeType === 1);
    return null;
  };
}
var atime = 0;
function mouseup(e) {
  console.log('mouseup ' + e + ' ' + e.target + ' ' + e.target.nodeName);
  tre = e.target.closest("tr");
  console.log('closest ' + tre + ' ' + tre.id);
  if (tre) {
    n = tre.id.replace(/\D/g, '');
    toggle(n);
  }
  // if (e.target && e.target.nodeName.toLowerCase() == 'tr') {
  //   // console.log('goto ' + e);
  //   // e.stopPropagation();
  //   // atime = new Date().getTime();
  // }
}
function goto(e) {
  // console.log('goto ' + e + ' ' + e.target + ' ' + e.target.nodeName);
  if (e.target && e.target.nodeName.toLowerCase() == 'a') {
    // console.log('goto ' + e);
    // e.stopPropagation();
    atime = new Date().getTime();
  }
}
var rowsel = -1;
function selectedtext() {
  text = '';
  if (typeof window.getSelection != "undefined") {
    text = window.getSelection().toString();
  } else if (typeof document.selection != "undefined" && document.selection.type == "Text") {
    text = document.selection.createRange().text;
  }
  return text.length > 0;
}
var selected = false;
function toggled(n) {
  selected = false;
}
function showimg(e) {
  var els = el(e).getElementsByTagName("img");
  for (i = 0; i < els.length; i++) {
    ds = els[i].getAttribute('data-src');
    if (ds && ds.length > 0) {
      els[i].setAttribute('src', ds);
    }
  }
}
function adde() {
  document.getElementById('rtable').addEventListener("mousedown", goto);
  document.getElementById('rtable').addEventListener("mouseup", mouseup);
  // var els = document.getElementById('rtable').getElementsByTagName("a");
  // for (i = 0; i < els.length; i++) {
  //   console.log('add ' + els[i]);
  //   els[i].addEventListener("mousedown", goto);
  // }
}
adde();
function toggle(n) {
  console.log('toggle');
  if ((new Date().getTime() - atime) < 250) {
    console.log('skip');
    return;
  }
  if (selectedtext() == true) {
    return;
  }
  if (el('r' + n).classList.contains('hidden')) {  // hide
    rowsel = -1;
    el('r' + n).classList.remove('hidden');
    el('r' + n + 'b').classList.remove('hidden');

    el('x' + n).classList.add('hidden');
    el('x' + n + 'b').classList.add('hidden');
    el('x' + n + 'c').classList.add('hidden');
    el('x' + n + 'd').classList.add('hidden');
    el('x' + n + 'e').classList.add('hidden');
  } else {  // show
    if (rowsel >= 0 && rowsel != n) {
      // toggle(rowsel);
    }
    rowsel = n;
    el('r' + n).classList.add('hidden');
    el('r' + n + 'b').classList.add('hidden');

    el('x' + n).classList.remove('hidden');
    el('x' + n + 'b').classList.remove('hidden');
    el('x' + n + 'c').classList.remove('hidden');
    el('x' + n + 'd').classList.remove('hidden');
    el('x' + n + 'e').classList.remove('hidden');

    showimg('x' + n);
    showimg('x' + n + 'b');
    showimg('x' + n + 'c');
    showimg('x' + n + 'd');
    showimg('x' + n + 'e');
  }
}

function update() {
  // --dtd--
  var t = 1596006000.0;
  var d2d = 660123.0;
  var delta = 6256.000000;
  // --dtd--
  var seconds = new Date() / 1000;
  var current = d2d + (seconds - t) * (delta / 86400.0);
  p = [ 1, 10, 25, 50, 100 ];
  for (i = 0; i < p.length; i++) {
    d = Math.floor(p[i] / 100.0 * current);
    // var ds = d.toLocaleString(undefined);
    var ds = String(d);
    var e = document.getElementById('p' + p[i]);
    var prev = e.innerHTML;
    e.innerHTML = ds;
    // e.classList.remove('change');
    if (ds != prev) {
      // e.classList.add('change');
    }
  }
  setTimeout(update, 500);
}
var show = 1;
var figures = 2;
function rotate() {
  show = show + 1;
  if (show > figures) {
    show = 1;
  }
  for (i = 1; i <= 2; i++) {
    var e = document.getElementById('c' + i);
    if (i == show) {
      e.classList.remove('hidden');
    } else {
      e.classList.add('hidden');
    }
  }
  setTimeout(rotate, 5000);
}
